Oil Market: Turpentine and Vegetable Oil from Zhejiang Report Price Increases

Turpentine from western Zhejiang is currently entering the market with new goods. Unexpectedly, the price of turpentine seeds has suddenly surged. Last week, the buying price for seeds was still only five yuan and fifty or sixty cents per dan, but recently, as various pressing workshops have started operating, the purchase price has increased to over six yuan, leading to higher costs. A few days ago, merchants from the interior came to Shanghai to sell over two hundred pieces of turpentine oil per railway car, offering a delivered price of twenty yuan and two cents per deduction. However, due to the sudden increase in seed prices, no one is willing to sell at this price anymore. Judging by the current market, the price is likely to be above twenty-one yuan. However, the Wuhan market has not yet changed. The Jinlan area of eastern Zhejiang has also seen price increases. Therefore, the market conditions in the north and south are gradually diverging. Local merchants, because of the new harvest season, have low inventory costs and initially thought that southern oil prices were reasonable. Now that price increases are being reported everywhere, they may shift their attention to Wuhan oil again.

Hardware: Native Nails Find Smoother Sales

Native factory nails (commonly referred to as native nails in the market) have recently seen more prosperous business. Customers from areas like Changjiang Road, as well as ports such as Ningbo, Fuzhou, and Wenzhou, are purchasing them. Furthermore, local construction teams, painters, and glass shops are all making transactions. Therefore, over the past two days, it is estimated that three to four thousand barrels have been sold. The price per barrel (one hundred pounds on a Tianping scale) is seven yuan and twenty cents for double-stranded nails, which is four or five cents cheaper than imported products. It is said that the supply of raw materials has been very low in recent days. People's confidence is strong, and the market is expected to increase significantly.

Free Talk

Youth and Lao Tzu

— Yi Zun

I heard that "ever since European culture spread eastward," Chinese morality has deteriorated, especially among modern youth, who often look down on Lao Tzu. This is likely a big mistake, because after seeing several examples, I feel that Lao Tzu is indeed very useful and beneficial to young people, not just as an aid to "literary cultivation."

There is an old article—I forget which book it's from—that tells us about a Taoist priest who possessed the art of immortality. He claimed to be over a hundred years old but looked "as beautiful as jade," like someone in their twenties. One day, this living immortal was hosting a grand banquet when suddenly an old man with white hair and beard came up to him asking for money. The Taoist priest scolded him away. While everyone was surprised, the living immortal said with emotion, "That's my young son. He didn't listen to me and refused to cultivate the Tao. Now you see, he's not even sixty yet and he's aged so terribly." Everyone was naturally very moved, but later they finally learned that the man was actually the Taoist priest's father.

There is also a new article that tells us about an ambitious person whose theories were very correct. He not only talked the talk but also walked the walk. However, when he saw old men suffering in some places, he thought of his own father. Even if his ideals were realized, it wouldn't make his father a master who didn't have to suffer. Therefore, he came up with even more correct theories, abandoned his original ideals, and became a filial son. If his parents had died early, how could his theories be so complete and grandiose? Isn't this also the benefit of Lao Tzu to young people?

So, is there no solution for young people whose fathers have already died? I think there is. There are still ways to figure it out. We still need to check old books. Another article—I also forgot which book it's from—tells us about an old woman who was begging for food when suddenly a wealthy man came up to her and said she was his long-lost mother. She took the opportunity and became an old lady. Later, when her son was marrying off his daughter, he and the old lady went to a jewelry store to buy gold jewelry. He took the items that the old lady had already liked to show his wife-to-be. Meanwhile, he asked the old lady to keep looking—but he disappeared from then on.

However, this is still like learning from the Taoist priest. You need to do it with real things. If you just make self-confessions, it doesn't matter if you really have a father or not. Someone previously advocated "virtual constitutional monarchy," so why not have "unparented filial sons" now? Zhang Zongchang respected Confucius, but his mansion probably didn't have the "Four Books" and "Five Classics."

Random Thoughts on Viewing Chrysanthemums

— Mu Mutian

Alone in a foreign land, I am a stranger,

Every holiday makes me miss my family even more.

I know my brothers are climbing to high places,

Wearing dogwood everywhere, missing one person.

This is a seven-character quatrain by the Tang Dynasty poet Wang Wei. Who doesn't know these four lines? Who isn't familiar with them? Writing them out, I think some enlightened people will say I'm "dumping garbage." However, today, facing these four lines, I feel a great longing.

I haven't been a good son. I haven't been a good brother either. Although my heart is good, they don't really understand. Not only am I always indifferent to my own family, but I also don't care much about my hometown. I feel that the best life is wandering. Living a wandering life in a foreign land is better than being bored "getting upset" in my hometown. Begging for food in a foreign land is better than being a landlord in my hometown. Although the country is now destroyed and the family broken, I still find the life of a small bourgeois in the city interesting.

Since returning to China, I have been gradually moving away from the café life. The sentimental and melancholic emotions of the past have also been uprooted in my heart. Maybe I'm just getting older. "Oil, salt, firewood, and rice" have gradually brought me closer to reality, making me realize that sorrow and depression are useless. Why drink coffee? Why drink wine? Although I shouldn't have gone down the path of writing, "since I'm here, I'll be content." Although I'm just a "half-empty bottle," I can still be somewhat useful. "Be a monk for a day, strike the bell for a day." Without a "monk," a "bald head" can also save a lost soul.

Recently, my mentality has been to live honestly, but today, my "heart has changed drastically." Going to school, seeing chrysanthemums everywhere, I feel an indescribable sadness. It's as if those chrysanthemums are all painted with blood. A few days ago, seeing news about "Chrysanthemum Festivals" everywhere, I didn't feel anything, but today, I feel an indescribable sadness. I miss the Northeast under the iron heel of imperialism. I can't help but recall Wang Wei's lines.

What's happening in the Northeast now? How are the people of the Northeast living in that fiery hell? I'm not exactly missing family, but I'm thinking of those hardworking farmers who have nowhere to turn. And in the Central Plains, are there still people appreciating chrysanthemums as if nothing has happened? I can't help but think of the phrase "only tranquility can lead to far-reaching things." At the same time, I think of the "Empty City Stratagem" even more. Perhaps the "Empty City Stratagem" is the Chinese people's specialty. However, now the imperialists probably don't have a marshal like Sima Yi who leads by example (tell you all, I saw this on the stage), so the "Empty City Stratagem" probably won't scare him. Try firing two cannons. What do we do then?

"The Dream of the Red Chamber" governs the country, "Golden Lotus" sells the home." It is said that this is the secret of the Manchu emperors. "Water Margin" and "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" are excellent military books. In particular, the "Empty City Stratagem" has been used countless times by a certain young marshal. The certain young marshal is not only good at singing the "Empty City Stratagem," but he has also reversed his father's militaristic ways and accepted Tolstoy's non-resistance doctrine. Moreover, he is thoroughly implementing it. I remember that a Japanese newspaper nominated him for the Nobel Peace Prize several years ago. I don't know if his name is on the list for this year's Nobel Peace Prize. However, today, I thought of the "Empty City Stratagem" from the chrysanthemums, and from the "Empty City Stratagem" I thought of a certain young teacher.

"Drawing a sword to cut water, the water flows more; raising a cup to dispel sorrow, sorrow increases more." The more I look at the chrysanthemums, the more unbearable my heart becomes. That's why I thought of Wang Wei's four lines. Today, I feel that these four lines have profound meaning. This is something I haven't experienced before.

Writing this, I recall seeing a Chrysanthemum Festival in Dalian City several years ago. Now, there is probably an even grander Chrysanthemum Festival in Dalian. Then, I remembered seeing a plan of "Manchukuo" and "Xinjing" in an illustrated magazine a few days ago, and I felt very sad, as if it were full of the blood of the "Manchu" people. However, today's mood is similar to that day.

But now, the armed people of "Manchuria" are still actively resisting Japan, right? Perhaps only they can save themselves.

Ganpu Correspondence (End)

— A Ying

Dear Brother □□

Anyone who has been to Ganpu probably knows about "Nanbei Lake." "Nanbei Lake" was originally named "Yongan Lake," about five miles from the west city. The form of this lake is the same as "West Lake," divided into north and south, separated by a long embankment, with pavilions and bridges, and tall "sidewalk willows" on both sides. Surrounded by mountains, except for the south, where the sea is. According to Mr. Wu Xiahu's "Ganpu" book, the lake's boundary has twelve li, a total of more than 3,700 acres, irrigating more than 8,000 acres of fields. Because it resembles "West Lake," it is commonly called "Little West Lake." However, compared to the two lakes, "Little West Lake" is not as beautiful as "West Lake," and it is really unavoidable to be "small," so that people's chests cannot be as open as they get on "West Lake." But there are also different places here from "West Lake," that is, there are endless tall trees on the mountains on three sides, and relying on the lake, there is a vast salt field, boundless sea: these cannot be found on "West Lake." If you want to take in these scenery at a glance, it is not difficult, just climb to the Jiujiu Peak, you can see the full view of West Lake: special is the crescent-shaped connected salt fields, thousands and tens of thousands of workers, if you are willing to approach it, you will gain a lot of experience, a good education. The problem is, what I know, is that most of the people who come here are visiting the lake, and few come to inspect the life of the salt area, as for understanding the suffering of the salt people, there is no need to talk about it.

I lived in the mountains north of this lake for nearly a month. I usually took a boat across the two lakes to the salt area in the early morning, and then rowed back in the evening. Of course, there are many things to record about the life on the lake, such as the lake and mountains in the moonlight, the fun of picking clams, the return journey in a storm, and some meditations caused by the changing lake scenery. But the joy is not my main purpose in coming here, and I don't want to touch on them one by one. However, there are some things that I can't forget. One is that the children on the lake, because of our short-term close life, are very shaken and very admired of the city. No matter where you are, you can see it. The city influences the countryside, this is inevitable, and the girls are really special and severe. I feel that this phenomenon makes the ancient and quiet air of a small "West Lake" very unstable. Here, I am delighted, I see how their psychology is gradually evolving, and how their expressions are gradually becoming tense. This picture, which is rarely clear and inevitable, allows me to see very deeply that I should state that the main reason is due to the influence of several women who came with me. Secondly, it was on the eve of my third departure from this place. That night, in order to commemorate the completion of most of our work, most people would not come again, and it was a clear night with a gentle breeze, and the lake and mountains were special. We hired four small boats and paralleled each other in the two lakes, rippling on the slight waves, and took a refreshing lake tour. I don't know why, in the laughter, autumn singing, and mournful sound of the xiao, I was reminded of an old poem. The full text of the poem is: "Drinking on the bridge on the bridge at midnight, all the people in the seat are heroes, and the stream flows silently in the moon. In the sparse shadows of apricot flowers, blowing the flute until dawn, the last twenty years have been the same. This body is still in surprise. I am free to climb up the small pavilion to see the new sunshine. How many things in ancient and modern times, the fishing songs rise in the middle of the night." I was humming this poem in a low voice, but I couldn't help but feel sad, and felt that the result of today's victory tour was just to increase the pain in the future. I even fell into a state of silence. However, further development of the thought, thinking of the poems written by Lu Fangweng, Wu Rulun and other ancient and modern poets, and even thinking about why they could not see from the development of society to recognize the joy of growth, only pay attention to the gathering and dispersal of individuals, for their own grief, and even could not help but be a little dumb. That night, I traveled in the lake for two hours, making all the salt people of "Xihaitou" wake up from their dreams in surprise, and ran to the shore of the lake to watch. In their eyes, we are not only living in a fairyland, but they know that although we have this moment of happiness, the suffering of struggling for survival is not the same as theirs?

Brother ○○, I can only tell you about the life of Ganpu in the correspondence here. There are many valuable materials and valuable life experiences, so I have to wait for the opportunity to write them out in the future.

Two Brothers (31)

— Written by Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

He lowered his head and ate again.

He wasn't hungry, he felt that nothing tasted good. He was eager to leave, to escape their conversation and jokes.

But Old Man Roland was now swayed by the aroma of the wine, and had forgotten his son's advice. He glanced at the bottle of champagne placed next to his plate, which was almost full. He didn't dare touch it, fearing new rebukes, so he thought of a cunning and clever way to get the wine bottle without attracting Biel's attention. He thought of a trick, a most common trick: he nonchalantly picked up the wine bottle, holding the bottom, stretched out his arm across the table to fill the empty glass in front of Biel; then he took turns filling the glasses of the others, and when it was his turn, he spoke loudly, although he poured a little into his own glass, others would surely say that it was accidental and due to lack of habit. And no one noticed this.

Biel unconsciously drank a lot. With an impatient temperament and a belly full of complaints, he often unconsciously took the tall glass, touched it to his lips, and through the glass, we could see many small bubbles running in the lively transparent liquid. He then slowly poured the liquid into his mouth, in order to feel the gas scattered on his tongue giving him a sweet little prickle.

Gradually, a gentle heat filled his body. This heat came from his stomach—which seemed like the furnace of this heat—reached his chest, occupied his limbs, and spread throughout his flesh, like a gentle and beneficial wave that brought happiness. He now felt a little more comfortable, not as impatient as before, not as dissatisfied as before; even the determination to talk to his brother about that matter tonight relaxed, not because he intentionally gave up on it, but because he didn't want to disturb the happiness he was feeling so quickly.

Boziru stood up and invited everyone to toast.

After bowing to everyone, he said!

"Ladies and gentlemen; we are gathered here today to celebrate a happy event for one of our friends. People used to say that wealth should be blind, but I thought it was just a little short-sighted or cunning. Now it has indeed made the son of Captain Roland of the Pearl, our loyal partner, prominent in Harbor."

After the speech, there was a burst of cheers and applause; Old Man Roland stood up to answer.

He seemed to have a little suffocation in his throat, and his tongue was not very flexible. After coughing for a while, he stammered:

"Thank you, Captain, I thank you on behalf of myself and my son. I will never forget your kindness. I toast in return."

His eyes and nostrils were filled with tears. He sat down, he had nothing more to say.

Now it was Zheeran's turn to speak, who was grinning;

"I should thank you here, loyal and elegant friends (he looked at Mrs. Lu), thanking you for giving me this moving proof of friendship today. But these are not a few words that can express my gratitude to you. In the future, at any time in my life, I will express my gratitude to you, because our friendship is not the kind of fleeting friendship."

His mother was very moved and said softly:

"Very good, my child."

But Boziru shouted:

"Come on, Mrs. Lu, you speak a few words on behalf of the women."

She raised her glass and said in a kind and slightly sad voice:

"As for me, I raise a glass to bless the spirit of Mr. Malaisha in heaven."

Talking About

A Study of Running Dogs

— Fu Ba

Judging by the character for "dog" (狗), its fate is not particularly good. The "Shuowen Jiezi" (說文解字, Explanatory Dictionary of Characters) under "dog" quotes Confucius saying: "Dog, to knock. Knocking at air to guard." From the two words "to knock" (叩也), we can imagine a state of wagging its tail and begging for pity, which does not seem very heroic. Further, from the "Erya" (爾雅, Approaching the Correct) which states, "Dog, not yet fully grown with hair" (犬，未成豪狗), it appears that a dog is simply a smaller version of a dog's cheek. Translated directly, it means "small dog," which in people's minds feels particularly insignificant, and even in a comprehensive zoological dictionary, it may not occupy a very high position.

However, as of today, this insignificant little dog has actually seen a great upswing in its fortunes, as if the Republic of China entered the "Dog Year" (戍運) in its twenty-first year. Thus, those who praise people call them "running dogs" (走狗), gamblers have greyhound racing (跑狗), and the Beijing Public Security Bureau Chief, in accordance with this "Dog Year" luck, issued a decree prohibiting women from keeping dogs. Recently, some busybodies in Shanghai have even formed a "Dog Beating Brigade" (打狗團). Although their intentions may differ—good, bad, supportive, or destructive—their attention on this dog is the same. Alas, the dog's luck can be said to be prosperous!

Ancient classifications of dogs were broadly divided into three types: The "Book of Rites: Subtleties" (禮疏) states, "There are three types of dogs: first, guard dogs, those that guard the home; second, field dogs, those used for hunting; third, food dogs, used to fill the kitchen with delicacies." The first type is the kind mentioned earlier that "knocks at air to guard," like the German Shepherd police dogs kept by modern wealthy people in their gatehouses. The second type is the fat and strong dogs seen on the streets today, with iron wire muzzles, either held by Westerners, wandering on the roadside, or sitting proudly in Ford automobiles. As for the third type, they were once cherished by General "Long Legs," and now, Shanghainese Cantonese restaurants occasionally sell a piece of it, called "Dog Leg" (戍腿). Notably absent from this list is the term "running dog." The term "running dog" first appeared in the "Yanzi Chunqiu" (晏子春秋, The Annals of Master Yan). The "Yanzi Chunqiu," in the chapter "Admonitions," records: "Duke Jing's running dog died, and the Duke ordered it to be provided with an outer coffin and inner offerings. Yanzi heard of this and admonished..." The term "running dog" first appeared in written records. According to records, Duke Jing, as the head of a state, was incomparable to General "Long Legs." The dogs he kept were certainly not food dogs used to fill the kitchen, but undoubtedly a modern Western-style Pekingese. This can be seen from the grandeur of its funeral—coffin and offerings. Alas, this is a dog hero!

Later, Fan Li, a minister of Yue, in his letter to Wen Zhong, wrote, "When the flying birds are exhausted, the good bow is stored away; when the cunning rabbit dies, the running dog is cooked" (飛烏盡，良弓藏，狡兎死，走狗烹), as recorded in Sima Qian's "Records of the Grand Historian" (史記). This marks the beginning of the term "running dog" being recorded in official history. It also appeared once in the unofficial history, "Strategies of the Warring States" (戰國策), both referring to a type of field dog. The reason why field dogs are favored is that they exist between humans and beasts, able to serve their masters. However, the ambiguity of their status also lies here. If you say they are beasts, they help humans slaughter their own kind; if you say they are human, they cannot change their original nature. They seem incompetent, yet they chase rabbits and deer, making a small splash; if you say they are capable, then they shouldn't be so obedient to human commands, content with a little leftover favor and self-satisfied. In short, it's difficult to determine, so let's leave it at that.

Generally speaking, before the Wei and Jin dynasties, the term "running dog" was not very common. After the Wei and Jin dynasties, through the poems and songs of scholars, running dogs filled the world.

The earliest article praising dogs is probably Bo Xuan's of the Jin dynasty. He wrote a "Rhapsody on the Running Dog" (走狗賦), whose memorable lines include: "Indeed, nothing is as swift as the eagle, nothing as fierce as the tiger, but the good dog's nature combines both strength and martial prowess. Seeking hidden traces, tracking lost trails, as swift as surging waves, as forceful as a startled dragon. Scaling mountains and crossing valleys, not leaving a rabbit in the plains, nor a deer in the forest. It is both swift and unmatched, and leisurely and measured." The thousands of words can be said to exhaust the art of praise. There are many such articles in later generations, so they are not listed here.

As for using "running dog" as a self-designation, some say it existed in the Han dynasty, but it can be reliably traced back to Zheng Banqiao of the Qing dynasty. Niu Yingzhi's "Rainy Window Notes" (雨窗消意錄) records: "Zheng Banqiao loved Xu Qingfend's poems the most, and once engraved a private seal that read, 'Zheng Xie, running dog under the gate of Xu Qingfend.'" This is also a unique way of presenting oneself. Alas, Zheng's affection for dogs can be said to be profound. From then on, the connection between humans and dogs became increasingly inseparable. Descending to modern times, there are many people who are willing to be running dogs to show off their refined tastes. Praising people often involves calling them "running dogs." It can be said that wherever there is well water to drink, the term "running dog" can be used. Fearing that people might forget their origins, I wrote this study on running dogs.

Modern Celebrity Calligraphy and Painting: A French Person Skilled in Chinese Painting, "Double Dragons"

A Scene of Romance

— Guang Han

Evening. Inside the library of ×× University. The surroundings are unusually quiet. A wisp of autumn coolness constantly blows in through the windows. Several students are buried in their work, each doing their own thing.

He and she occupy a table in the corner of the room, sitting across from each other, each with a book open, paper spread out, and pen in hand, writing.

Suddenly, he winks at her, passing a piece of paper he has finished writing. She takes it, says nothing, and writes one in return. He reads it and writes another one to pass over.

He and she lock eyes and smile.

He writes another one to pass over, and she writes another one to pass over.

He frowns slightly, and quickly writes another one to pass over.

She tears the paper to pieces and throws them under the table. He hurriedly bends down to pick them up, crumples them into a ball, and holds them tightly.

He glances at her and writes another one to pass over.

She just makes a few strokes on the paper with her pen.

A look of distress suddenly appears on his face. He puts down his pen, stretches, and lets out a long sigh.

She looks a little distressed and writes another one to pass over. Then comes a charming smile.

He sees it, and immediately his frown disappears. He nods, thinks for a while, and writes another one to pass over. He looks out the window.

"No!" she blurts out. The air in the room is shattered by the crisp sound. Several students who are reading look up at the same time, but after a while, they look down again, each doing their own thing. She is a little flustered, her face flushed, and she gives him a sharp glance.

He tries his best to calm himself down and writes another one to pass over.

She shakes her head and writes another one to pass over.

He looks at it, expresses his dissatisfaction, and immediately writes another one to pass over.

She ponders for a long time, looking very troubled.

He and she are silent for a moment. Everything becomes even quieter.

He suddenly gently grasps one of her hands, making a pleading expression. She looks a little scared, half-pushing and half-accepting, her head constantly looking left and right.

She pulls her hand back and writes another one to pass over. Amazing wrist.

He smiles, looking at her adoringly. She lowers her head shyly.

He makes a gesture. He and she put away their drawing tools, tear up the paper scraps, scatter them on the floor, and leave together.

It is getting dark, and the surroundings are still quiet. There are fewer people reading.

On a piece of scrap paper, these few words are scribbled: "Okay! I promise you, Brother ×!"

Page 21

Tuesday

— Yu Sheng

Wednesday, as usual, is the day for prisoners to be visited at the prison. Lianxian, who lives in the attic room, was already planning miserably the night before: cotton clothes are indispensable, the weather is unusually cold like this, the heavy snow is falling violently, and the north wind is like a knife scraping on people's faces, causing bone-chilling shivers. She thought of her husband imprisoned in the human hell, and her heart was broken!

She wandered the streets, buying a set of cotton clothes, and also bought a vegetable box. Back in the small building, she continued her busy work alone, lighting the prepared stove, preparing salty and durable vegetables; at the same time, she repaired her already old socks, and prayed gently in her heart. She thought silently that the things she had mended with her own hands could be worn on his body, and it would be the same as her being by his side, or it could give him some comfort! She also wanted to write a short letter, slip it into the clothes, and attach two dollars, fearing that he might need some pocket money.

When she started preparing to write the letter, her thoughts suddenly stopped, her throat tightened, and sour tears dripped onto the paper little by little. Heavens! What should she write? She pondered for a long time, and finally began to write with tears in her eyes: "Brother! I am here. I came after four days without receiving a letter. Hearing that you were arrested, my heart was so unexpectedly painful! Since things have come to this, there is no way to recover. At present, I only hope that you will take care, take care, take care the third time! I pray day and night that if heaven does not fail us, there will always be hope of seeing the light of day again. Endure everything, brother! I am sending two cotton quilts, a set of cotton clothes, and two pairs of old socks, which I have mended with my own hands. Every line of thread is connected to your sister's uncontrollable tears. There is also a box of side dishes, a toothbrush, toothpaste, and soap each, two small handkerchiefs, and two dollars for pocket money. Don't worry about me, my body is free and healthy! Lian Mei"

After everything was prepared, she fell into contemplation. She fantasized about the happiness when her husband returned in the future, and how she would cherish and love him more than ever before, like life itself! But, thinking again about the danger he was in now, she became timid, and the hope in her mind rapidly decreased to the lowest point. She also thought: it would be good to be sentenced to life imprisonment, as long as life is preserved! All kinds of fantasies, hopes, and fears disturbed and twisted her entire soul that night, and she did not close her eyes all night.

The snow was getting heavier and heavier, and the cold wind constantly pierced into her clothes. She packed the things she should bring, and repeatedly tightened the bulging abdomen. Because of the long journey from her residence to the "Black Terror" prison, she was protecting her nearly pregnant body, which was necessary.

The car was speeding on the bumpy and muddy road. In the desolate fields, there were no pedestrians. In the raging wind and snow, only she and the driver were the unfortunate ones among human beings! Ah! The boundless sorrow seemed to be borne on her heart and the driver's shoulders. In her heart, which was as fiery as an arrow, there was no time to think about anything, only eager to reach the cruel destination.

She lowered her head and walked into the tiger's mouth-like prison gate, registered at a small window, and returned to the corner on the left, leaning against the luggage and waiting on the cold and damp ground. Puddles of water were spitting bone-chilling cold air at her. Many prisoners with crushed limbs were being taken away for interrogation, passing in front of her, with haggard faces, painful hearts, and the clanging of shackles, breaking her entire heart little by little. She thought of her weak husband, how could he endure such torture? Her heart turned cold, her body trembled, and she clenched her hands tightly over her chest!

The soldiers came out with the roll call, and she immediately squeezed forward regardless. "Wang ××, Li ××!" "Chen Zhongxu, no visit allowed!" The soldier, wielding the power of life and death, called out proudly and seemingly angrily. "No visit allowed? Can the things be sent in?" "No visit allowed, of course, the things cannot be taken in." She was disappointed, as if she had fallen backwards from a cliff into a bottomless mountain stream! Finally, she begged a kind old soldier, who agreed to help her inquire, and after much pleading, the things could not be smuggled in either. She felt as if she had been saved, and waited patiently outside.

The luggage was brought out again, and the old soldier also had a sad expression on his face! She trembled as if she had seen a ghost, fearing that her hair would stand on end! She asked quickly: "What's wrong?" "He has been transferred to ×× yesterday, I regret that I can't help you!" "Really? Will it be dangerous to be transferred to ××?" She opened her eyes wide and asked. "To tell you the truth, he was secretly executed last night! And not just him." The sudden news was like a bolt from the blue for her, and she was shocked! Everything was destroyed, the last hope was also cut off, her breathing stopped, and she fell under the sycamore tree by the small pool. The wind was still raging, and snowflakes were hitting her pale face.

In this cruel world, she became a victim of love from then on.

Further Discussion on Vases and Vase Stands

— Jing Jia

Since writing the review on vases and vase stands, I had put this matter aside. Yesterday, I read Ms. Hua's article, and I have to cheer myself up and write some more. Although this is not like the "Wen Xuan" and "Zhuangzi" that can cause the world to turn upside down, at least, this is always an "interesting" issue, right?

The so-called "vase," it is said, is "because it looks good, used as a decoration, and has no practical use." Since the name "vase" is applied to female employees, then needless to say, female employees are "decorations" and have no practical use. Of course, I absolutely cannot say that "vase" is a term without any "humiliating" element. However, can ladies eliminate the insult of "vase" by coming up with the term "vase stand" to apply to men and women? Is this kind of Q-style mental victory a legitimate revenge?

Ms. Hua admits that there are "fake golds mixed in" among female employees. In other words, Ms. Hua admits that there are "vases" mixed in among female employees. We know that one rotten apple can spoil a basket of good apples, and a little ink can spoil a piece of white cloth. Because of the weakness of a few people, we are ridiculed as the "sick men of East Asia." We all know that to brush away insults, we must first start with ourselves. Who can say that shouting a few times after Japan occupied the Northeast provinces, "Damn Japanese dwarfs," can wash away our insults?

The person who came up with the term "vase," indeed, I believe he is cheering wildly and receiving praise. Because the term he came up with has been proven by facts. Of course, it is very joyful when one's thoughts can get the approval of the masses. I think Ms. Hua must also be very joyful, right? If the name "vase stand" can be as widely spread as "vase" as Ms. Hua wishes, shouldn't Ms. Hua raise a goblet and have a big drink? Since Ms. Hua knows that the person who came up with the name "vase" will not feel embarrassed at all, then shouldn't Ms. Hua be very happy for the name "vase stand"?

There are indeed quite a few modern male employees who are willing to prostrate themselves at the feet of modern female employees to wait on them. However, I believe that modern male employees will definitely not prostrate themselves before rural girls! A peacock will also display its feathers when it sees people dressed in gaudy red and white. Without vases, where do you put the flowers? Where do you put the stand?

If the name "vase stand" can be as widespread as "vase" as Ms. Hua wishes, not only should the ladies thank her for washing them clean, but even a man like me would prostrate myself at the corner of Ms. Hua's cheongsam and kowtow three times and bow nine times to express my endless gratitude. To be honest, ladies are always luckier than men and women. Female employees can still be a beautiful decoration, while men can't even be a decoration. In the organization, superiors will never scold female employees in person, at most they will say a few words behind their backs: "A vase is always just a vase," but men will be scolded by their superiors in person: "Rice bucket!" At least, a vase is always better than a rice bucket, right? Is there no "humiliation" in the name "rice bucket"? If Ms. Hua can promote men from "rice buckets" to "vase stands," isn't that enough for me to be grateful for?

If we want to talk about equal rights for men and women, I really don't know how to say it well. Since the Shen Bao has had self-employment introductions, someone has statistically shown that 90% of the responses are occupied by women. The budding of women's occupations is the withering of men's occupations! Who can deny it?

If Ms. Hua feels quite satisfied and comforted after having the name "vase stand," then I wish her to be satisfied like that forever!

Page 22

The Sorrow of Students

— Zu

The days have passed so quickly, and it is the beginning of the end of November again. This spring, due to some reasons, I dropped out of school and studied at home. Ah! A whole year is about to be wasted just like this! So-called self-study, where is the result of self-study? I still remember when I was in school, the Chinese teacher gave us a topic in composition class to write: "The Importance of Self-Study," "The Value of Learning Lies in Self-Study." It is said that way, but how difficult and not easy it is to implement! At that time, we all said this (that is, now, there are still many people who say this: "School life is too rigid, the distance between school and social reality is too far too far!") Since this is the case, then the awakened students who have recognized this shortcoming should be how to strive to enthusiastically use society as a school to start learning the practical knowledge that meets social application. However, how easy is it to talk about it! This chaotic contradiction, a society where everything presents an unstable phenomenon, what it gives to us general youth is simply cruelly squeezed and called us to be suffocated to death, where can there be the opportunity for us to study ourselves?

Because of age, although the environment and my ideals are absolutely contradictory, but, because it is contradictory, we only want to work hard to study for a few levels, but the first thing that shows me a warning is the ghost thing "diploma". I can't get this thing, I can't jump over this difficult gate that is being checked strictly. I wear this ghostly thing, of course, makes me feel extremely sad! However, at the same time, I recalled the past, and it made me start to have great doubts about school again! Scene after scene of farcical plays are still clearly reflected in my memory: about the year of the third grade of junior high school, the "teacher" was very careless in class, we students, were still young, knew something, the "teacher" was careless, I was happy to "write freely", before the "teacher" came to class, we wrote on the blackboard, "Talk casually", the "teacher" listened to us the most, so at that time he was also a strange and cute person in our minds. So during class time, everyone talked casually. In the past, when it came to monthly exams, as long as we all said "can't write", the "teacher" would do it for us on the blackboard, and they would copy it, and everyone would get 90 to 100 points; or, if the teacher was stricter, they would try to move the school servant who printed the exam papers, or after the exam, go to the "teacher" to steal it and revise it, or everyone pass or copy the important things in advance on small notes and desks ... The tricks were played as much as possible. In this way, after messing around in school, I got a false transcript. Now, I feel very empty in my heart. Thinking like this, waves rose in my brain again; I thought, even if I could go to university, the biggest doubt would still lurk in my heart: after graduating from university, will I definitely be able to achieve my aspirations? Will I definitely be able to solve my life problems? The factual answer: there are many college graduates who have returned from studying abroad and are unemployed?

Ah: all kinds of things hidden in my heart make people worry: in the past, I entered "Mama Hu" school, and now I feel that everything is empty: I want to seek some practical learning, I resolutely left school and wanted to study myself, I wanted to make up for it, but the result was disappointing, I wanted to step into the door of the school again, but because of the diploma, it hinders my enterprising heart: I opened my eyes wide and looked at the group of unemployed people, the very obvious university students and overseas students also joined, and it made me tremble with fear! Ah, the sorrow of students! The sorrow of youth!

Novel

Childhood Fragments of Memory (7)

— Lie Huo

However, Mother, after hearing this, uttered a set of persuasive words: "I heard that the county magistrate is an old friend of Teacher Du. There's no question about Teacher Du getting a position in the government office! At least nine out of ten chances are reliable. Go, go! Teacher Du's wife, please don't say such discouraging words, lest Teacher Du hears them and lose heart!" As soon as she finished speaking, she gazed at me and touched my bald head. "You are Teacher Du's disciple, so work hard, and you may also go to the government office in the future! Look, your eldest brother didn't work hard, and it turned into 'Burning cow dung, nothing accomplished' [Note 5]. Your father lost heart and didn't have the courage, so he left your second, third, and fourth brothers at home to handle hoes. You must work hard! Handling hoes is tough, like a beast of burden!"

"Yes, Little Five, you must work hard, so you can also go to the government office in the future, which will be much more comfortable!" Teacher Du's wife laughed heartily.

After Teacher Du's wife left, Mother went to cook lunch.

From then on, the entire village's elementary students began to fear losing their education. The parents were busy searching for a teacher, and they found a Mr. Liu. I still don't know Mr. Liu's full name to this day, but I can still vaguely remember his nickname: "Loose Antique," and some also called him "Shorty Pine." However, the former was more commonly used because he was indeed quite antique in character, and although he wasn't short to an extreme degree, he was still an inch or two shorter than the average person.

This Mr. Liu was indeed a bit odd. He always had puffed cheeks and a mournful face. Sometimes he would smile, but it was a bitter smile. It was said that when he was young, he had some intelligence and was very good at memorization. At that time, people said that he had the hope of passing the children's exam. However, when he went to take the exam, he ran into bad luck and "failed the exam." Therefore, he was quite frustrated. When talking about the examiners, he would grumble a few words, saying, "They are some things with no eyes!" After saying this, he seemed to feel much better, and then he would smile, with the bitter smile probably stemming from this. However, he did not lose heart because of this. Instead, he worked even harder. He desperately picked up a complete Four Books and read it over and over again, memorizing all the annotations. However, he took the exam again, three times, and countless times, but he was still Mr. Liu in a long cloth gown, and the red button on the official hat still did not develop a liking for his scalp. This made him frustrated to the point of being dumbfounded. As a result, he didn't even have the confidence to write clear and coherent letters for the neighbors (Note 6), even though he was very familiar with the complete Four Books.

However, the people in the village still had a strong belief in him, as devout as women's belief in Guanyin, saying that he was the only great Confucian scholar within dozens of miles. They would ask him for advice when they had something to do, and writing letters was a given. They were especially happy to send their children to him to study.

When the "rice-harvesting break" was over, Mr. Liu's private school opened its doors. Father sent me there. "After finishing the Analects and Mencius, we'll read the Great Learning later. Let's start reading Elementary Learning now!" Father offered his opinion to Mr. Liu. Mr. Liu didn't quite agree. His opinion was this: "The Five Classics and Four Books are the words of the sages,"

"The ultimate purpose of the great Dao is in them, so they must be read! As for Elementary Learning, it is inevitably a bit vulgar. It's okay for merchants and peddlers to read it, but for a Confucian scholar to read it would be a waste of time!" Father replied evasively: "Yes, I just want to have him become a peddler, so he's studying Elementary Learning! If Mr. Liu has time, please explain the Analects and Mencius to him in detail."

The matter was quickly decided, and I began to read Elementary Learning.

Film Special

A Few "Bit Players" Regarding Hollywood (Part 1)

— Xi Wen

A big star's every frown and smile, every sigh and cough, are all worthy of being printed in large letters in newspapers and magazines, making us linger and admire them. But a big star is not a big star simply by performing a solo act. As the saying goes, a beautiful peony needs green leaves to support it, and a general achieves fame on the backs of ten thousand corpses. There are leading actors on the stage, but the play cannot be performed without those who carry flags and hold umbrellas. Therefore, in a film, in addition to the big stars, there must also be many supporting actors. Among the supporting actors, there is one group that we most easily overlook, but which is very important: a group of "bit players." No film can be made without bit players and be entirely taken care of by the stars. Even star-studded films like "Grand Hotel" and "Dinner at Eight," which will soon be coming to Shanghai, cannot be entirely composed of famous stars. Therefore, these "bit players" are like extras on the stage, not important but indispensable. For example, if Greta Garbo is sitting in a beautiful car, there must be a chauffeur. That chauffeur is a bit player. When Clark Gable runs into a bar and gets into a fight with a drunk, that drunk is also a bit player. Chauffeurs, robbers, politicians, laundresses, policemen, and all other minor roles that appear briefly in the film and then disappear are called bit players.

Although they are bit players, they each have their own specialties. Those who play doctors always play doctors; those who play priests always play priests. They never get mixed up. And because they always play the same role, over the years, they become familiar to the audience without realizing it. So we often see someone in a film and unknowingly shout, "Isn't that the doorman from that other film?" And they themselves specialize in one role, becoming skilled through practice and playing it perfectly. I will now name a few of the most famous bit players so that you can pay a little more attention when you watch a film next time. Even if you don't want to remember their names, recognizing their faces is very interesting.

The first and most famous bit player is Eric Mayne. You are guaranteed to have seen him many times. His specialty is playing doctors, priests, lawyers, and diplomats because he has a long beard, curly hair, and a distinguished appearance. Because he is serious in demeanor, he can play experts of all kinds without looking like an amateur. As for his background, he is Irish and studied theology at Westminster in London. Strangely, he later gave up theology and went into acting. He excelled in Shakespearean operas, and he is still a Shakespearean drama lecturer at the Los Angeles Public Library. Unfortunately, he is too out of touch with the times. He has fallen from being a leading actor on the stage to a bit player in films. In addition, he had very bad luck; his wife died, and both of his sons were killed in the European war. He became a lonely old man, living in a small hotel in Hollywood and often going out for walks alone. He is neatly dressed and dignified in demeanor, and one can tell at a glance that he is an English gentleman, but who would know that he is a marginalized and heartbroken person? (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "The Mystery of the Wax Museum"

— Ling He

The Mystery of the Museum 丨 Grand Theater Screening 丨

It is a most obvious fact that American films strive for perfection in form. This certainly proves that they have made great progress in technology, and at the same time, in order to develop their business, they must also have good forms to attract audiences. This is true of musical films, and it is also true of horror films outside of musical films.

Speaking of horror films, we immediately think of "The Mummy," which uses the resurrection of ancient corpses as a gimmick, and its allure is conceivable. But because of its absurdity and lack of foundation, it will inevitably be rejected by progressive audiences. Because of this, smart filmmakers have to look for materials that can replace the supernatural outside of the "supernatural." "The Mystery of the Wax Museum" is undoubtedly Warner Brothers' clever trick. The filmmaker exaggerated the assassination event as much as possible in order to obtain the same magic as the supernatural.

However, our requirements for stories are the truthfulness and universality of the story, and in terms of the content of this work, we cannot obtain the completeness of the above two conditions. This can be proved by examples.

We certainly acknowledge that under the structure of real society, everything is a commodity, and so-called art is also a disguised form of commodity. Therefore, it is not contradictory to the current social system for wax figure makers to use all methods to seize profits. At the same time, the playwright tells us that sculptors are ultimately not easy to support and can only set fire to their own works in an attempt to obtain compensation from the insurance company. But we have to ask, why must this sculptor use the corpses of modern people as models when he wants to sculpt portraits of ancient people? This is very far-fetched. Moreover, the wax figures he sculpted in New York are the same as those sculpted in London. Does this mean that the ones sculpted in London also use corpses as models? This is enough to prove that the playwright, in order to make this sculptor kill people, tried his best to come up with this very far-fetched reason and construct this untrue and bizarre story, even if it exists, it is very accidental and not a true portrayal of daily life.

Therefore, we can prove that it is indeed not easy to make money with film art, especially in this time of financial panic and weakened purchasing power. Although the propagandists must say in grand terms that this is "an attack on the dangers of modern art trends," what we understand in the film is the exposure of the madness of the producer himself! It is certainly dangerous to use human bodies as molds to make wax figures, but it is even more dangerous to use such a bizarre story as the content of a work.

Speaking of horror films, we immediately think of the makeup of "The Mummy," and the magic of that makeup is truly admirable. Here, the method of using rosin to glue the face is used in the same way. It is true that the sculptor Yegud's face becomes so terrifying after being burned, but this cannot be achieved without advanced makeup techniques. (The Mummy's makeup embalms corpses, while here, the makeup is for people with burned faces, which should be more reasonable than the former.) At the same time, Frederic March's makeup in "Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde" and Lon Chaney's makeup as a thousand-faced man are sufficient to illustrate the progress of theatrical art in science.

Speaking of the thousand-faced man, the acting skills here are similar to those of Lon Chaney. Lion Alwill is also worthy of great praise. When he was in the burning wax museum, he watched his beloved wax figures melt and be destroyed one by one, and that profound expression gave us the most powerful impression. In addition to the ugly face he disguised, the original appearance of Yegud was also very good. Naturally, there is a symbolic meaning in the fact that the woman "breaks" the mask to reveal the ugliness, but it is not very appropriate in terms of reason. If she "scratches" it, it would show that the mask is soft, because wearing a hard mask all the time would not be realistic and have lively expressions.

Speaking of acting again, the female lead Glenda Farrell is truly a comedic genius. Her fluent speech and lively performance are just right, but her name is not on the poster, while Fay Wray, who is not important, is used as promotional material. This shows the contradictory phenomenon in business, naturally because Farrell is not as famous as Wray. We don't have to belittle Fay Wray because her role is not important, but she is still equal to her role in "The Most Dangerous Game." Among the other supporting actors, the one who played Spryluk (the sculptor's assistant) also performed very well.

The director's skills, like those of general horror films, are very capable of grasping the audience's tense emotions. In particular, using a happy crook to write this tense plot feels like a new and lovely approach. As for the climax of the first part and the final climax, they are both handled very appropriately. Among them, there are certainly many terrifying scenes that use mechanical sets or make people suspicious and fearful to deliberately create a shocking effect, but things like the croaking of toads and the discovery of whiskey in an open coffin are very clever.

Because it is a color film, it feels more beautiful in form. The best are the displays in the wax museum, the burning of the wax museum, the theft of corpses in the funeral home, and the hanging of彩 at the New Year. If it were not in color, the above scenes would never have achieved such results.

Finally, one more sentence, the film production skills of American films have indeed made great progress, but their capital is also really not small!

"Wild Camellia" Reviews "Maid of The Mountain"

— Moore

Since criticism that emphasizes ideological concepts is generally regarded as "formulaic" criticism and is rejected indiscriminately, this crisis will inevitably destroy correct film criticism if it develops further. Therefore, in one context, I emphasized the ideological aspect of film art. Naturally, form is determined by content. Precisely because form is determined by content, those who can truly grasp the ideological concepts of film will inevitably solve its form. In current foreign films, we often see exactly the same form (this is certainly not in the narrow sense), and this complete sameness of form must be because its content has something in common. (This is certainly not a mechanical reference to the story.)

"Wild Camellia" is a so-called "martial arts musical" film. If we only vulgarly introduce its form, then not to mention the readers, even ordinary "critics" will be deceived by its form. Because until now, new "artistic concepts" have not yet been established among our general "critics." We can only start from the aspect of meaning to expose the toxicity of form.

The producer of "Wild Camellia" is suffering from the harm of officials, just like all modern citizens. Therefore, in this film, he created a "chieftain" to play with the newly arrived and tyrannical governor. He deliberately wrote the "chieftain" as very outstanding. The "residents of the town" "plead for help" because of the tyranny of the new governor. This shows that the "chieftain" was invited by the people, is for the "people," and not for "profit."

However, our producer, although resentful of the officials at the time, does not feel resentful of the social system that promotes the tyranny and corruption of officials, and the laws that do not give the people the right to dismiss them, but deeply supports it. Therefore, he does not use the power of the people to dismiss or reject this tyrannical new governor, but makes the people beg the "chieftain" for help. At the same time, he puts the release of the captured "chieftain" not under the power of the people, but under the effectiveness of the old governor's powers, which still have ten minutes left; this shows that our producer is a thorough and complete supporter of the old system and old laws.

In terms of the story itself, some places are not clear.

First, before the new governor takes office, the people know that he is a tyrannical official, and even if he has been an official elsewhere, the people should not seek help from the "chieftain."

Second, since the "chieftain" has tied up the new governor and disguised himself, how can the people in the place who know that the new governor is tyrannical not recognize the new governor at all? If the people love the "chieftain," then the "chieftain" should naturally be more familiar to the people. Why must they wait for Tuo Sha's announcement before capturing him?

Third, since the tyranny of the new governor is known to all, the old governor naturally knows it too. At the same time, the old governor also hates the tyranny of the new governor and releases the chieftain. Why did he release him later and then capture him earlier?

There is no need to mention other small places.

Because this story has many songs and dances, the director has overlooked many places and deliberately lengthened the song and dance scenes, which can naturally make this film more "sexy," but it also makes it more vulgar.

Under this story, the actors naturally have a lot of acting to do, so everyone is working very hard!

The Nursery in "Life"

The shooting of "Life," directed by Fei Mu of Lianhua Film Company, is now nine-tenths complete, and the entire film can be completed soon. In this play, the lives of the two women played by Ruan Lingyu and Lin Chuchu are extremely rough. Ruan Lingyu wanders and roams throughout her life, and Lin Chuchu lives with children throughout her life. A scene of a nursery was shot indoors a few days ago. Xing Shaomei bought a large number of cradles and children's supplies in advance. Lin Chuchu was made up as an old woman, and her demeanor was very vivid. The office staff of the nursery are all old men with white hair and beards. Because this scene required a large number of babies, many women gathered in the photography studio with their children before the shooting began. When the shooting began, they happily put their children in the cradles, which was very interesting, but because the children were separated from their mothers, they all cried loudly, but because of their crying, several exceptionally wonderful shots were filmed.

Film Novel The Weakness of Women My Weakness (5)

— Fusheng

Lorna came in. He told Lola Morning that she was about to meet Gilad. Lola asked him why he had to meet him at the fashion exhibition. Lorna said that he never went to any public gatherings, but the Ting Fashion Exhibition was something he couldn't miss, because he was the deputy manager of the Gregerie lingerie company. For the sake of business, he couldn't not go. So Lorna taught her some tips on how to deal with Gilad. He had two special hobbies. One was eating raw carrots, and the other was old stamps. He said, "You should tell him that you also like old stamps. If it comes to the point where you have to, you might as well eat some carrots. I know this is too difficult for you, but..." Lola said softly, "As long as Lorna tells me to, let alone eat carrots, I will swallow his entire set of old stamps." Lorna said, "You have to find a way to make him kiss you... Come, I'll teach you, this is something women can't teach!" Lola thought that kissing Lorna shouldn't be taken too seriously, because it was just like dancing or playing golf. Lorna didn't really want her to kiss him. But when Lola shyly pursed her lips, how... it seemed like it was real. Lorna smiled, "Lola, do you know yourself, you kiss really well."

The next night, Lola and Iv stood on the stairs, looking down at the noisy exhibition below. She supported Iv, her hands were cold, and her knees were shaking. They watched many models walking on the stage in various fashions. The French tailor Lanier was squeezing around in the crowd. Suddenly Lanier stopped and talked to a thin, middle-aged man with glasses. Iv pulled Lola tightly and said to her, "The one with glasses is Gilad Gregorie, the deputy manager of Gregorie lingerie company." Lola looked over and saw Gilad, she shuddered. Diana encouraged her from the side: "You can't desert at the last minute. You have to know that if you don't do well, Lorna will become a poor man."

Before going downstairs, Iv, Maureen, and others taught her a lot of gossip. So they went downstairs. Lorna introduced Lola to Gilad. Gilad stared blankly at Lola, revealing a very silly look. Lola almost laughed, but she held back and pretended to be very dignified and said to Gilad: "Why don't we go out to the veranda and count the stars in the sky?" Gilad immediately agreed with her and walked out. He told Lola that he liked to watch the stars in the sky very much: he had counted the stars in the sky one day, and there were a total of 12,308. As they were talking on the veranda, Lola heard the sound of turning silk from behind the flower pots, knowing that Lorna and those women were eavesdropping there. Okay, let them listen. So she said to Gilad: "Lorna is extremely annoying to me. He only knows women, and has no other abilities besides that!" After Lola finished speaking, she vaguely heard Lorna's angry scolding, and she was very happy in her heart. (To be continued)
